## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) — nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration determined by restoring forces and damping/forcing terms, typically modeled as dv_dt = f(x, v, t) for nonlinear harmonic oscillators (e.g., Duffing, van der Pol, driven/damped systems). The variables x (position), v (velocity), and t (time) match standard second-order ODE oscillator forms rewritten as a first-order system.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude conservative motion)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator in a linear medium)
- Constant + linear forcing bias: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 (gravity/bias or constant actuator offset)
- Harmonic driving force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodically driven oscillator)
- Parametric stiffness modulation: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric excitation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger geometric/material nonlinearities)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) velocity drag: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag / nonlinear dissipation)
- Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (self-excited oscillation models with amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- van der Pol oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit-cycle behavior)
- Liénard-type general oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2 + c3 * x**4) * v (broad class covering many nonlinear damping laws)
- Nonlinear pendulum (sine restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle pendulum-like restoring with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force often depends on x only and is an odd function for symmetric potentials: dv_dt ≈ f(x) with f(-x) = -f(x) (e.g., x, x^3, sin(c*x)).
- Dissipation typically enters as terms proportional to v (linear damping) or v*Abs(v), v^3 (nonlinear drag), and should oppose motion on average (effective sign against v).
- Self-excited/limit-cycle oscillators often have state-dependent damping where the coefficient of v changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c0 - x^2)*v or (c0 - v^2)*v.
- External periodic forcing appears as additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms; resonance/lock-in behavior is associated with such explicit time dependence.
- Parametric excitation modifies the stiffness multiplying x (or occasionally damping multiplying v) as a periodic function of t, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness is indicated by the sign of the x**3 term: +x**3 tends to increase frequency with amplitude; -x**3 tends to decrease it.
- Energy-like structure: if dv_dt has no v-dependent terms, the system is closer to Hamiltonian/conservative dynamics; v-terms indicate non-conservative energy exchange.
- Geometric nonlinearities often manifest as bounded restoring forces (sin(c*x)) rather than unbounded polynomials, suggesting saturation in the restoring torque/force.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO6)
============================================================
GT: -beta*log(Abs(v) + c0) - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `-0.661172493025524*v - 1.16984597672115*x**3 - 0.330586246512762*log(Abs(v) + 1)`

Key features of GT:
- A term proportional to `x**3`
- A term proportional to `v`
- A term proportional to `log(|v| + 1)`
- No dependence on `t`
- No other terms (no `v**2`, no constants, no exponentials, no sin/cos)

The critical issue is `log(|v| + 1)` vs `log(v + 1)`. Since `v` takes both positive and negative values, `|v| + 1 ≠ v + 1` in general. So candidates with `log(c*v + 1)` cannot match `log(|v| + 1)` unless they have additional terms to compensate.

Let me also note: candidates with extra terms can potentially match if those extra terms' coefficients can be set to zero. Terms like `v**c` with free `c` can potentially be set to duplicate existing terms (e.g., `v**1 = v`).

Let me analyze each candidate systematically:

**For each candidate, I need to check:**
1. Can `t`-dependent terms be zeroed? (set coefficients to 0)
2. Can extra terms be zeroed or merged?
3. Does it contain `log(|v| + 1)` or can it produce it?

Since `v` takes both signs, `log(c*v + 1)` ≠ `log(|v| + 1)` for any constant `c`. This is a fundamental mismatch. Only candidates that somehow produce `log(|v| + 1)` can match.

None of the candidates contain `Abs(v)`. The candidates with `log(c*v + 1)` have `v`, not `|v|`. Since `v` takes both positive and negative values, these are fundamentally different functions.

Candidates WITHOUT log terms need power-law or exponential terms to replicate `log(|v|+1)`, which is impossible due to linear independence of these function families.

Let me verify: Can any combination of `v**c` terms for various `c` values exactly equal `log(|v|+1)`? No - power functions and logarithms are linearly independent.

Can `exp(c*v)` produce `log(|v|+1)`? No.

Can `sin(c*v + d)` produce `log(|v|+1)`? No.

Can `(c + v)**5` produce `log(|v|+1)`? No.

So the only candidates that could potentially match are those with `log(...)` terms, but they all have `log(c*v + 1)`, not `log(|v| + 1)`.

Since `log(c*v + 1)` is defined and smooth near `v=0` but `log(|v|+1)` has a kink at `v=0` (its derivative is discontinuous), no smooth function can equal `log(|v|+1)` for all `v` in a neighborhood of 0.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT** because none contain `Abs(v)` and the GT's `log(|v|+1)` term creates a non-smooth function that cannot be replicated by any of the smooth basis functions available in the candidates.
